## \#1 Posted by: Eboosted Posted at: 2017-11-12T06:30:55.652Z Reads: 1930

```
Hello guys, I've been offering Loaded Vanguard enclosures for a while now, but as I build more boards I have other enclosures for sale as well, so I'm making a thread with my enclosures portafolio:

I have several requests to make a Loaded Vanguard 12S enclosure, for all those who would like the benefits of a 12S battery whether you are building a new Loaded Vanguard with loads of range, torque and speed from the start or want to upgrade your current vanguard equipped with 10S, this is the perfect time.

Personally since I tested 12S, I can't go back to 10S anymore.

12S Vanguard Battery enclosure
US$ 70
Here is a comparison between the 10S and 12S battery enclosure.
```

## \#10 Posted by: Eboosted Posted at: 2017-11-28T04:54:08.712Z Reads: 1157

```
I'm trying to build a 10s6p and a 12s5p for people that have requested it.

However, I'm finding a lot challenges in order to have a nice sweet enclosure that look perfect, I could do any type of enclosure but not all of them will seamlessly blend with the deck.

If there's an option that would fit 60 cells but won't be visually appealing, I definitely won't ever build it. 

A two cell layer enclosure will look terrible and would have a really bad ground clearance, unless you make an enclosure boost board like with two segments. 

Runing cell horizontally would allow me to run a 10s6p or 12s5p but there wouldn't be any space left for the switch, BMS, wires, xt60 or xt90 connectors, maybe only for tow VESCs or Focboxes.

You could plan to run the VESCs on a different  compartment on the top of the deck, as on a Trampa EMTB,  and the connect the motors, but if wouldn't be a 12s5p enclosure anymore. 

<img src="/uploads/db1493/original/3X/d/9/d92848006b718003e3c5cd9654f027301a7ebcbe.jpg" width="281" height="500">

If you try to run the cells vertically, almost no deck in the market will allow 10 cells vertically, you will have to get a deck with at least 9" on the thinnest part, that's a pretty fat deck, so that's also not an option.

<img src="/uploads/db1493/original/3X/3/9/393941f2ed2685c7ceff7dc61531167f7917d981.jpg" width="281" height="500">

<img src="/uploads/db1493/original/3X/5/5/553037b73d0becb9be79cba68a8febc66f28b0a4.jpg" width="281" height="500">
```

## \#37 Posted by: pshaw Posted at: 2017-12-15T17:28:33.326Z Reads: 803

```
This^ !!!!!!!!! Alan I looked at the bottom of my deck closely and the shape side to side is pretty basic. Just slightly curved downwards towards the edges. So little than when screwing it down it would probably flex right against the small curves. 

The real issue is if the enclosure including flat parts is more than 24inches end to end. Then you start getting really into the drop where you‚Äôd almost have to have the deck to design it. I don‚Äôt suppose fiberglass will bend very much and mold to the deck contours.
```

## \#55 Posted by: Eboosted Posted at: 2017-12-16T06:15:21.744Z Reads: 745

```
@deckoz wrapping your batteries with kapton tape will create too much heat inside the pack, if you have the means to control heat inside the batteries it would be ok, otherwise I suggest to remove some kapton and use heat wrap.
```

## \#67 Posted by: psychotiller Posted at: 2017-12-17T14:25:12.039Z Reads: 742

```
Large enclosures are 2 pieces because they have to be...I've tried to explain that but I'm not sure if you understand why.  A 33" oven only gives about 22" of space to put a sheet of plastic in there. Then there is the rack in the oven that holds the frame, that holds the hot plastic...You end up with 20" max if you get a good form because it's hard to stretch a mold all the way to the edges of your sheet and still get a good seal.

There are vaccuum forming machines that can be ordered with a max plate of 27". We may order one. But until then, 2 piece abs enclosures are a necessity not a choice.

But for the record. There is nothing fuctionally wrong with 2 piece enclosures the way I do it.
```

---

## \#121 Posted by: Eboosted Posted at: 2017-12-24T14:52:04.237Z Reads: 602

```
12 packs of 4 parallel each, connected with dual 12awg soldered wires. 

<img src="/uploads/db1493/original/3X/f/4/f40e230a12d61f75a700fe80369eb7eb1d2a3ad2.jpg" width="666" height="500">
<img src="/uploads/db1493/original/3X/6/8/681ff3306e2e905c34f2f44cb9181959edaa3cd1.jpg" width="375" height="500">

The wires run through the center of the enclosure which have a lower profile than the perimeter where the rubber gasket sits on the deck.
```

---
## \#122 Posted by: Sender Posted at: 2017-12-24T15:44:12.661Z Reads: 576

```
Thank You! Awesome work! So the gasket itself is giving the middle section enough standoff for the silicone wires, brilliant! Did you make any other changes compared to your first.... "Tragic Trampa"?
```

---
## \#123 Posted by: Eboosted Posted at: 2017-12-24T16:23:14.691Z Reads: 580

```
Well, even though if you don't use a gasket the center dividers are lower than the borders, so there is plenty of space for thick wires to connect the packs. 

On this build, the Phoenix, I won't use bullet connectors buy xt90, so if they unplug and connect again due vibrations they won't spark just disconnect. 

I would also use an antispark switch with fuse kindly donated by Atilla @esk8, I owe you a big one my friend

I will also stick the packs with the enclosure with 3M double sided tape so they don't move, mitigate the vibrations and allow an easier disassembling for inspections.

I will use a 12s balance monitoring system with buzzer from Mtech shipped FROM Germany with the help of my friend  @nowind

The deck will have 1 ply more than the urban carver deck to reduce the flex a bit and reduce the flex of the battery.

I'll start a build log as soon as I have the board runing on the streets
```

```
Great work. Are the same material as the others? Seems much more flexible.

[quote="Eboosted, post:123, topic:38073"]
I will also stick the packs with the enclosure with 3M double sided tape so they don't move, mitigate the vibrations and allow an easier disassembling for inspections.
```

## \#127 Posted by: Eboosted Posted at: 2017-12-24T18:20:22.392Z Reads: 555

```
[quote="Flaco, post:126, topic:38073"]
Great work. Are the same material as the others? Seems much more flexible.
[/quote]

Yes, the same material but with the segments it ended up being pretty flexible.

[quote="Flaco, post:126, topic:38073"]
What if you stick it to the deck instead with something like 3M Dual Lock, wouldn't that unload the enclosure?
[/quote]

It's better to have the weight of the batteries at the bottom because it's the natural state of the beard and it'll stick better with time.
```

## \#132 Posted by: Eboosted Posted at: 2017-12-30T06:58:17.181Z Reads: 599

```
For all those who needed a procedure to mount enclosures here is the one I used that gave me great results:

The holes must be drilled when you have your enclosure on hand, I never ship them predrilled because it's almost impossible to make a perfectly aligned hole after a predrilled one. 

This is the correct procedure:

1. Cut 4 small pieces of double sided tape put them on the border of the enclosure, where it'll touch the deck

2. Align the enclosure on the deck where you want it to be and stick it

3. Mark the drilling points with a pencil, use a ruler for accuracy

4. Drill the holes through the enclosure and deck with 5mm brad pointed wood drll bit

<img src="/uploads/db1493/original/3X/a/e/ae96d8a01e215b69f67faa09a8227b55a1da0c03.jpeg" width="443" height="332">

5. Remove the enclosure and drill a 7mm holes on the deck only, to allow the mounting of the nut inserts. 

6. Install nut inserts from top to bottom, turn by hand until you can't get them in more. 

<img src="/uploads/db1493/original/3X/b/a/ba4a021b2f8b39ca89210d3d6d4f903b60a4134f.jpg" width="666" height="500">

7. Screw one M5 bolt on the nut insert completely and then keep turning until the nut insert is completeky flushed to the deck surface, thus will help you to make a perfect thread on the deck without braking the nut insert itself (do not screw the nut insert by using an Allen wrench directly without doing this procedure first, of the muy interesante will brake) 

8. Remove the bolt and nut insert

9. Reinsert the nut insert again from top to bottom, this time with the Allen wrench, it will go down smoothly, without forcing it or braking 

10. Install enclosure with M5 bolts from the bottom

No template needed at all, perfect fitment

<img src="/uploads/db1493/original/3X/2/d/2d8f028c2f82f2c9472e4d2ed88b9719f538c638.jpg" width="374" height="500">
```

```
@barajabali here is your custom 12S3P for 20700 Sanyo 30A batteries and quad FocBox

This was a clever design, you can actually have more discharge on a 12S3P on Sanyo 20700 (90A) against a 12S4P on 30Q 18650 (80A)
```

## \#421 Posted by: GrecoMan Posted at: 2018-04-21T14:14:38.079Z Reads: 384

```
is there a reason you went socket head instead of countersunk? i love my countersunk washers, the socket head ones were a little too chunky for me
```

---
## \#422 Posted by: mikenyc Posted at: 2018-04-21T14:16:57.143Z Reads: 379

```
Mmm gold!

10c
```

---
## \#423 Posted by: Sender Posted at: 2018-04-21T14:18:42.009Z Reads: 385

```
I went socket because I feel like they lock down better. Probably just in my head (and that is what @Deckoz did, and he is my hero).
```

---
## \#424 Posted by: Deckoz Posted at: 2018-04-21T14:18:56.506Z Reads: 365

```
I used socket head Because I like the depth of the heads, less likely to strip, or had the head torqued off. Counter sunk are also typically wider when in combination with a fender washer. So size was a thought too. Using M4 socketheads with fender washers is the perfect width for eboosteds flanges.
```

---
## \#425 Posted by: GrecoMan Posted at: 2018-04-21T14:19:49.796Z Reads: 354

```
@Deckoz do you guys really torque down your enclosure enough that you strip the bolts?
```

---
## \#426 Posted by: Deckoz Posted at: 2018-04-21T14:20:28.482Z Reads: 370

```
No... But I use the m4 throughout the build.. motor mounts. Motors etc. Easier to buy packs of 200 and use it throughout. As motor mounts and motor screws are always socket head on my build... More so multipurpose purchasing..
```

---
## \#427 Posted by: Sender Posted at: 2018-04-21T14:26:15.904Z Reads: 371

```
For me its what Decky said.  But Also, I like the socket style because it just feels more secure to me.  I own a rock climbing gym and some of the holds we put on the wall use socket bolts and some use countersunk bolts.  The ones with Martini bolts spin more (we dont like that).


I know this doesn't compare to this application at all, but just why I have that mindsight.
```

---
## \#428 Posted by: GrecoMan Posted at: 2018-04-21T14:55:16.675Z Reads: 369

```
i had the same problem with holds spinning in my friends gym with socket and countersunk, you just need more bolts üòä
```

## \#437 Posted by: taz Posted at: 2018-04-21T20:04:12.601Z Reads: 384

```
What is the thickness of that enclosure?
```

---
## \#438 Posted by: Deckoz Posted at: 2018-04-21T22:57:51.290Z Reads: 389

```
Additional, at the peak(center of the deck), it's an additional 26mm @taz. Measuring the thickness detached doesn't tell the whole story. As when I torque it down the enclosure pulls itself outward and flatter. I.e when I lay the enclosure on without bolting it. I can push down in the center and there is a gap. Once I bolt it, It pulls the enclosure outward with less of a curve and compresses the batteries against the deck.
```

---
## \#439 Posted by: taz Posted at: 2018-04-21T23:04:10.549Z Reads: 385

```
Thanks. That is really thin so less spacers are need to provide the necessary clearance.
```

## \#469 Posted by: Deckoz Posted at: 2018-05-11T13:37:45.147Z Reads: 398

```
[quote="Kug3lis, post:466, topic:38073, full:true"]
@Eboosted do you also do custom enclosures?

Yes he does...

Thats how the
- EVO, soon Falcon
- Icarus
- Zenith
- Spud

Etc came to be. Normally he requires a minimum request quantity so that making the molds is worth it. I believe Minimum is 3 or 5 enclosures, and needs the deck to make the initial bucks & mold. 

Pretty sure his current options are

- Landyatchz Evo
- Landyatchz Evo Falcon (coming soon)
- Sector 9 Bintang
- Hi5ber Zenith
- Loaded Vanguard, 10s and 12s options
- Loaded Icarus 10/12s
- Never Summer Reaper
- Trampa Street Carver bottom mount
- Trampa HS11/Holy Pro bottom mount
- Jet Spud 29"
- Universal Flat enclosures 10s, 12s

Most have been commissioned by forum members :) and his work is amazing... You've seen my Evo enclosure ;)
```

## \#609 Posted by: osbor Posted at: 2018-06-16T07:25:10.408Z Reads: 347

```
what's the normal timetable for 12s univeral enclosures?
i put an order in on the 10th, just would like to know if it's a several day or several week thing.

```

---
## \#610 Posted by: Eboosted Posted at: 2018-06-16T16:53:58.716Z Reads: 354

```
@osbor it depends on what enclosure you request and the currently available stock.

For instance I usually have stock in TX location, if this is the case shipping to USA takes 3 days.

If there is no stock I make it by hand in Lima and it takes around 7 days, then you need to select international parcel 15-20 days to ship or for USD 30 more you can select DHL (2 days international).
```

## \#629 Posted by: Eboosted Posted at: 2018-06-20T23:44:42.556Z Reads: 399

```
This other enclosure is very special because it was requested by @bigboytoys the same week he past away, so it was designed and manufactured with a lot of pasion to detail and plenty of love.

Trampa HS11 DS
[img]https://i.imgur.com/tn5vqnW.jpg[/img]

It's not as thick as I though and it should hold double stack of cells for a crazy 12S8p, 11S8P if you want to run quad motors.

[img]https://i.imgur.com/PABuWGE.jpg[/img]

I changed the design for a more symmetrical/eye-pleasing one, now it has a big compatment on the sides where you could mount a big BMS for charge and discharge and two rows of cells, the sides are bigger as they are less exposed to flex forces.

[img]https://i.imgur.com/xw0nDQs.jpg[/img]
[img]https://i.imgur.com/RTxTHPR.jpg[/img]
[img]https://i.imgur.com/CggphXS.jpg[/img]
[img]https://i.imgur.com/eBO61R7.jpg[/img]
[img]https://i.imgur.com/1fCeeIw.jpg[/img]

I'd say it's perfect for those who are looking for a big battery but dislike the big box between both feet.
```

## \#654 Posted by: bigben Posted at: 2018-06-24T20:00:22.321Z Reads: 371

```
I know a lot of people don't like the bottom ones. I have found them usable though if you get the hole size right, countersink them slightly and back them out a little every other turn as if you were cutting a thread. (which in effect you are!)
```

## \#659 Posted by: Eboosted Posted at: 2018-06-25T17:01:29.399Z Reads: 378

```
Even the bolts will back out, you need to use loctite.

Velcro is a really bad idea from my point of view, taking the enclosure appart will force it too much and you will end up with both sides of the velcro in your hand.

Besides the velcro won't stick back with the same strength

Even though there are not much things under de deck, take into consideration the continuous vibrations on everyday use, you won't believe how much stress the holding points had to bear.
```

## \#689 Posted by: Andy87 Posted at: 2018-06-28T09:16:20.299Z Reads: 373

```
If to use epoxy only on the front and back it shouldn't be too much.
You don‚Äôt need to fill all area. Just restrict the area you fill out to the frame. Like 2cm or so.

On the sides big neoprene should be enough.
 
If you have access to a 3D printer you could print a layer for the front and back. Or just take some wood, cut it and file it till it fit our needs.
```

## \#694 Posted by: Mikenopolis Posted at: 2018-06-29T02:38:04.142Z Reads: 379

```
[quote="never4getf150forums, post:693, topic:38073"]
about 2.50$ per box
[/quote]

I‚Äôm not sure how shipping works in Lima or other countries. In the US, FedEx has free boxes. I‚Äôve shipped out 5 decks so far with those boxes. Just get that large or medium one. Open it flat and flip in around so becomes a plain brown box. Do the same with two more boxes, taper the ends of the middle box by cutting the end flaps and connect the boxes together. Pad the ends, then tape up the whole thing. ![image|436x500](upload://vHWLIrBsU19SfBsACpNeW91Lqyf.jpeg)
```

## \#698 Posted by: never4getf150forums Posted at: 2018-06-29T03:15:32.076Z Reads: 359

```
yeah but you can use the 1095 box eitherway, since Alan sends it thru USPS priority mail..

the problem comes with flat rate boxes, those can't be folded/cut up/ changed from their original shape if you use the same company to ship them.

the 1095 box is essentially a free box shipped to your house you can fold in anywhichway and still ship it since it's not flat rate.
```

## \#699 Posted by: Eboosted Posted at: 2018-06-29T03:39:30.185Z Reads: 362

```
@osbor I'll post it here as well, other people might benefit from it. 

Try heating the part when the enclosure needs to bend with a heat gun, give it just enough heat so it doesn't deform too much. 

Buy a can of spray matte black paint in order to make it look brand new after the process.

Even though these have been painted with acrylic paint you can use this brand and it matches the color perfect, you can get it at Walmart.
```

---

## \#704 Posted by: Eboosted Posted at: 2018-06-29T06:08:04.047Z Reads: 367

```
On these new inserts you need to use epoxy, let them dry overnight otherwise they will strip. 

I see the heat gun truck worked but the paint cracked, I suggest you buy some sandpaper and paint it with matte black spray paint, it will look perfect.
```

---
## \#705 Posted by: osbor Posted at: 2018-06-29T06:12:41.505Z Reads: 360

```
Use epoxy how exactly?
Drill the 7mm hole, put some epoxy in the hole, then press the inserts in and remove the excess epoxy?
```

---
## \#706 Posted by: Eboosted Posted at: 2018-06-29T06:16:24.951Z Reads: 363

```
Yes. But use the epoxy around the inserts, press them on the deck until they are fully flat to the surface, do not remove the excess until the next day when they are really hard and brittle this way you could just crack them out with a flat screwdriver and a hammer
```

## \#771 Posted by: chris.hunt Posted at: 2018-07-25T23:04:54.101Z Reads: 379


---
## \#772 Posted by: Eboosted Posted at: 2018-07-26T01:48:54.267Z Reads: 391

```
@chris.hunt yes, for a Vanguard 10S enclosure you need this layout.
![e1621d3d-0392-46a6-a2ba-2e158967e9f7|690x388](upload://uvAxo6siYoiKX4qxNhAPb8T71NW.jpg)
![aea3c23c-1b9b-4978-beaf-ad54534d7e82|281x500](upload://6uePFUQp0j3DHpdv7HuSoBZOx1H.jpg)
![54a55f4d-6a9d-4809-8772-bba1d82b4c34|690x388](upload://5Gadk0LXWPv2o1CoIJDa5a6MBp3.jpg)

@gmurad if you want a truly high discharge battery you need the Sanyo [20700A](https://www.e-cigarette-forum.com/threads/sanyo-20700a-30a-3100mah-20700-bench-test-results-a-great-performing-30a-3100mah-battery.784543/)
 30A discharge not the [20700B](https://www.e-cigarette-forum.com/threads/sanyo-20700b-4000mah-20700-bench-test-results-a-peek-at-the-future.775809/) which has a maximum discharge of only 16A.
```

## \#788 Posted by: TinnieSinker Posted at: 2018-08-05T12:25:10.476Z Reads: 385

```
@osbor is it weird to reply a month later? probably
I had the same problem, didn't realise the deck I ordered was drop down :flushed: but i love them both so i made it work.

sanded down the edges, mostly on the corners to make it sit closer. made this thing out of wood to hold the motor wires.

+1 for neoprene but wouldn't mind something a bit more rubbery. I find that once it's squished it takes a while to un-squish.

also, +1 for loctite. i lost a screw because I was too lazy to re-apply after opening it a few times ...whooops!

![IMG_20180512_162932|666x388](upload://ruNMAWoG7TBu44X55kddmn7mBhM.jpg)
![IMG_20180805_215355|666x500](upload://tZ6w8fBoUBdmrYSy7V0iWKOjz9b.jpg)
![IMG_20180805_220316|375x499](upload://rKX0kBs6LEricDA6HqpuZWcAIRy.jpg)

for anyone complaining about minor imperfections, I can assure you it won't make a difference after the first ride. :joy:


![IMG_20180805_215446|666x500](upload://6jQLWBE7TaQSBFDadmrDF3FifHr.jpg)
```

## \#796 Posted by: uigiroux Posted at: 2018-08-10T13:47:24.049Z Reads: 351

```
The 40T and 30T are the same size, both 21700.  Also the 30T has a higher discharge at 35A and 3000mAh, while the 40T is 30A but 4000mAh.  Personally I'd go with the 40T over the 30T for the extra capacity.  I don't think the extra 5A discharge the 30T is capable of will make much of a difference, they're both putting out a ton of power, more likely that they'll rarely need to be working at full power... or whatever you would say, lol.  I'm terms of size though, I think the new Sony VTC6A is something that should strongly be considered.  It's a 3000mAh cell and 25A.  That's pretty close to the larger sized cells power but still in an 18650.  I'm keeping my eye out for that one :wink:
```

---

## \#814 Posted by: Eboosted Posted at: 2018-08-18T23:00:01.526Z Reads: 352

```
I'm super excited. After weeks of design, thowing design to the trash and go back to the drawing board I finished the Moonshine Sidekick enclosure, an enclosure for the most beautiful deck I ever had, it has the best characteristics perfect concave, perfect 35" length which makes it very portable but not much so it has a great stability for high speeds, has a useful kicktail and a sweet shape.

The enclosure was a challenge because I needed to fit a 10S4P at least and kicktail decks do not have much space between the trucks, you could also fit a 10S5P but you will need to mount some electronics on top of the battery but it has some space space to do so.

https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=QjOY5SJwVmA
```

## \#840 Posted by: Jc06505n Posted at: 2018-08-23T18:11:31.187Z Reads: 316

```
Then I advise relocating the BMS to get that space back. Also , you should put neoprene besides and below the enclosure to ensure that the components are moving around so much and to form an absolute gap between the enclosure and deck

edit: 

>Alan the BMS isn‚Äôt on top of the cells you realise? It‚Äôs at the end‚Ä¶

Ah in that case the problem is most likely the slightly bigger cell sizes adding up . While you might lose some clearance (nothing smallrisers wont fix) neoprene is the way to go
```

## \#846 Posted by: never4getf150forums Posted at: 2018-08-24T09:48:10.492Z Reads: 312


---
## \#847 Posted by: mrjonnyjones Posted at: 2018-08-24T09:53:55.966Z Reads: 326

```
Approximate dimensions that I found on [IMR Batteries](https://www.imrbatteries.com/)...

**Sony VTC6:** 18.5mm x 65.2mm
**Samsung 30Q:** 18.33mm x 64.85mm

So they are slightly larger, but really not by much. Multiplied, though, it could have a snowball effect and create a slightly larger battery overall compared to using 30Q cells. This is what I'm a little annoyed about, but I'm sure there's a way around it... even if Alan can create a new enclosure that I'd happily pay for... however I could be being naive with regards to tooling etc.

With regards to Alan not knowing Sony cells wouldn't fit, for sure there would be something written on the website... I guess this is a learning curve for us all :rofl:
```

---
## \#848 Posted by: darkkevind Posted at: 2018-08-24T10:08:41.249Z Reads: 329

```
@never4getf150forums @mrjonnyjones

Yes, all 18650 cells have a variation in size from one brand to another. I thought it was more than this but having measured the two is seems the 30q are only 0.5mm smaller than the VT6, so I imagine is not the issue here...

What's weird is that there is so much gap in this instance, even more gap if you line the enclosure with 1-1.5mm of sound and vibration deadening neoprene.

I've pointed @mrjonnyjones in the direction of some 6-8mm rubber strips that can be used to make a gasket in this instance.

But for future reference @Eboosted, personally I'd make the enclosure at least 5mm deeper to allow the user to use neoprene on the deck side, as well as the inside of the enclosure.
```

---
## \#849 Posted by: Eboosted Posted at: 2018-08-24T14:07:27.956Z Reads: 307

```
I'm working on a taller enclosure right now with 10mm more height this might alleviate this issue. I'll keep you posted @mrjonnyjones
```

## \#902 Posted by: Eboosted Posted at: 2018-09-19T06:18:09.240Z Reads: 328

```
[quote="Skunk, post:870, topic:38073, full:true"]
Loving the sidekick enclosure. I‚Äôve only seen the pictures of it on a blank deck.
Any with trucks and wheels?
Can you mount the motors forwards?
[/quote]

On the first version of the enclosure and 83mm wheels I wasn't able to mount the motors forward:

[img]https://i.imgur.com/py1hMeO.jpg[/img] 

I'm doing a modification on the enclosure and moving everything more towards the nose, this will give me enough space to mount dual 6355s belt driven system. 

I'm also designing a 12s5p moonshine sidekick enclosure that could hold a big 80A Bestech BMS for charge and discharge and vesc6s
```

## \#926 Posted by: niuva Posted at: 2018-09-24T18:33:30.505Z Reads: 317

```
Can the [Landyachtz Evo Falcon Enclosure](https://www.eboardsperu.com/product/landyachtz-evo-falcon-enclosure/) fit five [2s4p N.E.S.E modules](http://18650.lt/index.php/2s4p-n-e-s-e-module/), 
 (totaling up to 10s4p) BMS (Approx. 53x63mm) and [Focbox Unity](https://www.enertionboards.com/focbox-speed-controller/focbox-unity-dual-motor-foc-controller-esc/) ? 

BMS: 53x63mm
FocBox Unity: 19x68x117mm
N.E.S.E 2s4p module: 22x74x188mm (with bolts on both ends)

Knowing the diameters of the enclosure interior space would be of great help. :slight_smile: 
If so, I'm buying it!
```

---
## \#927 Posted by: Eboosted Posted at: 2018-09-24T19:21:26.452Z Reads: 303

```
On the top of the Evo you have 185mm of width on the bottom part, just above the vesc compartment, you have 150mm of width. So unfortunately a 10s4p made of NESE modules won't fit on the Evo enclosure, Focbox unity will fit perfectly as well as the BMS. 

Nese modules take too much space, you are better off buying a boss lever spot welder, make a 12s5p and save money at the end, you just need to loose the feeling of fear to the challenge
```

---

## \#933 Posted by: Eboosted Posted at: 2018-09-26T05:15:51.643Z Reads: 305

```
I'm really impresssed, I forgot to tight the trucks and went for a test ride I though I was going to have speed woobles but realized that even with the trucks extremely loose it was very stable even at full speed, WTF :scream:

I made short stop and adjusted only the rear truck and the stability was improved even more, the good thing is you can turn a lot on low speeds, you just need to press you heal/toes further down and it would turn around a  coin.
```

## \#946 Posted by: jaatis Posted at: 2018-09-30T14:25:19.911Z Reads: 301

```
@Eboosted Did you change the design (height) of the Vanguard 10S4P enclosure based on the few complaints about battery packs not fitting? On your website there is now a VTC variant of the enclosure but is the "normal" one changed in some way as well?
```

---
## \#947 Posted by: Eboosted Posted at: 2018-09-30T14:59:27.939Z Reads: 303

```
The Vanguard 10s4p enclosure is the enclosure I have sold the most and had no complains in the past however if you are going to mount a a 10s4p made of Sony Vtc6 you need to choose that variant which has more height because those cells have a higher diameter than regular cells.
```

---
## \#948 Posted by: jaatis Posted at: 2018-10-01T14:16:59.395Z Reads: 317

```
Just out of curiosity I measured multiple cells of VTC6's and 30Q's and many of the VTC6 cells were actually thinner or the same diameter. There was as much difference between each brand's cells as there was between Sony and Samsung cells, if that makes sense. So in general I wouldn't say VTC6's are bigger.

Anyway I'm definitely considering your beautiful enclosures for my next build :slight_smile: 

![20181001_170104|690x435](upload://zZAKRSr1ePyVZOXDHHXfE51VGOn.jpeg)
```

## \#1004 Posted by: Blacksheep Posted at: 2018-10-17T05:39:28.152Z Reads: 304


---
## \#1005 Posted by: Eboosted Posted at: 2018-10-17T05:40:21.199Z Reads: 320

```
[quote="craj1031tx, post:1003, topic:38073"]
Why is the HS11 preferred over the other Trampa decks
[/quote]

The Trampa HS11 was a really nice deck because it had no holes on the center, this was good for waterproofing the battery pack and electronics, the carver deck is nice too but it sits to high from the ground for my taste, looks a bit goofy, the hs11/HolyPro 35 looks like a race car close to the ground. Lastly, the HolyPro 35 deck is the same as the HS11 but you need to cover the holes with fiberglass or epoxy, the result is also nice but some people won't buy it because of this, if you use urban thread tires the looks is awesome, low but not as much so you can run over all speedbumps on the street.

Here is my trampa holypro 35 with holes covered and urban threads, I love it:

https://youtu.be/fbltK7MG-qE

Hope this answers your question :slight_smile:
```

---

## \#1028 Posted by: trancejunkiexxl Posted at: 2018-10-19T16:29:21.758Z Reads: 309

```
Do share I've been riding and gathered a bunch of Nix that I would like to fill in paint I would love to know what materials you are using ‚ò∫
```

---
## \#1029 Posted by: Eboosted Posted at: 2018-10-19T17:17:41.497Z Reads: 335

```
Buy these:

Automotive car filler:
https://www.amazon.com/Bondo-Professional-Filler-Weight-233/dp/B000FCGT58/ref=sr_1_1_sspa?ie=UTF8&qid=1539968451&sr=8-1-spons&keywords=bondo+filler&psc=1

This exact brand and color of spray paint in Walmart:
![c644fb19-c889-4b64-86af-be0f5fd0356f|281x500](upload://cUcgjs87NkDmMQ8YIhQe7LjENOT.jpeg) 

Flex Putty knife:
https://www.amazon.com/Warner-ProGrip-Putty-Knife-90131/dp/B0062P6N1M/ref=sr_1_1?s=hi&ie=UTF8&qid=1539969512&sr=1-1&keywords=Warner+1-1%2F4%22+ProGrip+Full

One sheet of high grit and one of low grit count sand paper:

1. Sand the part you need to cover and clean it
2. Apply car filler with the putty knife, let it dry well
3. Sand it down with low grit and finish it and detail it with high grit
4. Clean the surface and apply spray paint 20cm away from the target and let it dry

Enjoy a brand new enclosure whenever you want even though you have scratched it over curbs :sunglasses:
```

---

## \#1091 Posted by: Eboosted Posted at: 2018-11-16T00:28:52.753Z Reads: 302

```
I wonder where are you guys getting the NCR20700A batteries these day, they are still pretty expensive and difficult to source. The NCR20700B have a pretty lame maximum discharge rate for a battery that big, good capacity though
```

---
## \#1092 Posted by: Colydog Posted at: 2018-11-16T00:46:03.486Z Reads: 312

```
https://batterybro.com/products/sanyo-20700-b
This is where I got mine. The price per Wh is a bit higher but the package shape means I can get a 17Ah 10s 4p in  400mm of battery length instead of say a 30q pack with 15Ah 10s5p taking up 450mm of battery length. 2mm thicker and 10 mm wider to gain that much battery capacity in a shorter pack, that's still got for around 80A, That's worth the few extra dolarydos for me.
```

---
## \#1093 Posted by: Eboosted Posted at: 2018-11-16T19:37:41.601Z Reads: 300

```
On the 20700B you can only get 15A on each cell for a total of 60A on a 12S4P form, discharge is too low for a Carver deck with pneumatics from my point of view. I rather use a 12s4p made of Samsung 30Q 18650 or even Sony VTC6 instead for 80A discharge.

If range is very important to you a better choice would be a NCR20700A, that on a 12S4P array will give you a craxy 120A of discharge, that'd be EPIC!
```

---
## \#1094 Posted by: Eboosted Posted at: 2018-11-17T21:41:53.089Z Reads: 315

```
The Moonshine sidekick DS enclosure is ready :grinning:

Can't wait to try this beast on the board, it has a lot of room for a full size BMS and 2 VESCs 6.

As the Sidekick is a motorcycle inspired deck I came up with a a grip tank bike design for it:
[img]https://i.imgur.com/MKs4lIr.jpg[/img]
[img]https://i.imgur.com/IH3ZFyd.jpg[/img][img]https://i.imgur.com/JLllq9v.jpg[/img]

The enclosue is able to hold more than 60 18650 cells, however a 12S6P would be perfect if want to run a full size BMS even the BIG ones plus two FocBoxes.

[img]https://i.imgur.com/y1HjfJU.jpg[/img]
[img]https://i.imgur.com/UOWkmVM.jpg[/img]
[img]https://i.imgur.com/kNK1GpR.jpg[/img]
[img]https://i.imgur.com/AyVmamt.jpg[/img]

If you want to go crazy and need extremely long range you could fit a 10S8P, completely unnecesary for everyday use but there are a lot of insane guys around here so they might find this a pretty nice starting point.

At the bottom I left a flat surface in order to allow an ESC aluminum heatsink fitment.
```

## \#1113 Posted by: erikringsmuth Posted at: 2018-11-25T22:28:33.380Z Reads: 311

```
I'm new here (first post) and am trying to spec out my first build. I want to do a Loaded Vanguard build with a slight variation from other builds I've seen here. I want to use the FocBox Unity combined with the eBoosted enclosures and 10S4P battery.

* FocBox Unity https://www.enertionboards.com/focbox-speed-controller/focbox-unity-dual-motor-foc-controller-esc/
* eBoosted 10S4P battery https://www.eboardsperu.com/product/10s4p-battery-for-loaded-vanguard/
* eBoosted BMS https://www.eboardsperu.com/product/bms-for-charging-10s/
* eBoosted power port https://www.eboardsperu.com/product/dust-proof-power-port/

I don't have any electrical experience so I'm wondering what's involved wiring this up. @eboosted the battery says it comes with a XT60 connector and the BMS mentions it includes the labor for wiring the balance leads to the battery.

If I get this setup, do I just need to connect the battery XT60 to the FocBox XT60 or is there other wiring I need to do?

Thanks, Erik
```

---
## \#1114 Posted by: tardyparty7 Posted at: 2018-11-25T23:14:54.488Z Reads: 290

```
I talked to @eboosted in the past. You need to wire your own BMS, but to be honest, soldering shouldn't be that hard. You can pm him and talk about including an anti-spark switch and charging port.
```

---
## \#1115 Posted by: Eboosted Posted at: 2018-11-25T23:42:12.120Z Reads: 298

```
I will wire the balance leads of the BMS for you, this is the hardest part, you will only need to locate the charging port where you want it and run the negative to the BMS and positive to the battery. 

The battery will have an xt90 so you just plug it to the unity to the extension wire on one end, (you need to make it yourself as the length needs to be measured on your own build) and the unity at the other end. 

It's extremely easy to do that
```

---
## \#1116 Posted by: erikringsmuth Posted at: 2018-11-26T00:03:59.026Z Reads: 296

```
Awesome! Sounds simple enough to me.
```

## \#1118 Posted by: Eboosted Posted at: 2018-11-29T23:40:53.490Z Reads: 321

```
So today I'm releasing the Evo 39" DS V2.

The difference between this and the V1 is the length of the nose and tail which gives you more room for inwards motor mounts for both 4WD and 2WD applications.

[img]https://i.imgur.com/TtnS9kX.jpg[/img]
[img]https://i.imgur.com/YIrpaQ1.jpg[/img]
[img]https://i.imgur.com/HWMibZI.jpg[/img]

[img]https://i.imgur.com/vvpujQM.jpg[/img]
[img]https://i.imgur.com/U6nXeEC.jpg[/img]

As you can see it has the same central shape as it's prececesor but still wraps the microdrop but will give you more room.

This enclosure should hold a 12s8p no problem

@mackann shipping tomorrow
```

## \#1208 Posted by: Odysseus Posted at: 2019-01-09T15:47:14.556Z Reads: 299

```
Hey guys, I'm in the process of mounting the ESC enclosure to my Vanguard Flex 1.

I'm just a little unsure of the placement. Does this look ideal, or would you recommend it being closer to / further from the motor?

I'm a little worried about the wiring getting too stressed whilst turning, and subsequently wearing out. ![20190109_173731|281x500](upload://xlOEBGiLeQeci82ahBG2pbn16Z8.jpeg)
```

---
## \#1209 Posted by: J_Dizzle Posted at: 2019-01-09T16:28:41.943Z Reads: 289

```
Hello @Eboosted what length screws and washers should I use to mounts my enclosure on the vanguard?
```

---
## \#1210 Posted by: Pedrodemio Posted at: 2019-01-09T16:53:43.296Z Reads: 283

```
This is the worst way to make the wires exit the motor, they will short in no time due to the insulation wearing out

The best is to exit them facing the hanger and do a large bend and them route into the enclosure, also is good practice to hold the motor wires to the mount as soon as it exit the motor, this way it can't get damaged by rubbing into the motor itself

About the enclosure position, you can put it closer to the motor, just make sure you still have a gap when turning hard
```

---
## \#1211 Posted by: Eboosted Posted at: 2019-01-09T17:01:15.870Z Reads: 279

```
@odysseus position it a little lower so the shape of the deck follows the outline of the ESC enclosure, but take into consideration the motor mounts won't touch the enclosure on full leans. 

M5 x 20 works good on the Vanguard
```

---
## \#1212 Posted by: hiboute Posted at: 2019-01-09T17:43:52.813Z Reads: 275

```
Double stack of 20700 or 18560?
```

---
## \#1213 Posted by: tardyparty7 Posted at: 2019-01-09T17:48:31.655Z Reads: 282

```
you should face the motor the other way so the wires are closer to the trucks if the wires are too long.
```

---
## \#1214 Posted by: Eboosted Posted at: 2019-01-09T21:38:53.673Z Reads: 282

```
[quote="tardyparty7, post:1213, topic:38073, full:true"]
you should face the motor the other way so the wires are closer to the trucks if the wires are too long.
[/quote]

I suggest you don't do that if you want to attract too much attention, inwards mottors will give you not only a sleeker look but it'll be very easy to grad the front frucks and carry it like a carry-on luggage.

Wire your phase motors differently, look the forum for pictures
```

---
## \#1215 Posted by: b264 Posted at: 2019-01-09T22:06:40.150Z Reads: 270

```
Run the wires from the motor back towards the truck, then turn and go to the ESC.  It's less flex and wear on the wires.
```

---
## \#1216 Posted by: Odysseus Posted at: 2019-01-09T23:00:54.956Z Reads: 282

```
Also, I ended up using M4 x 20, which seem to have done the trick.
```

## \#1220 Posted by: Eboosted Posted at: 2019-01-11T04:11:48.371Z Reads: 313

```
At last, finally I finished the Loaded Kut-thaka enclosure, I chose to make a DS from the begining which can hold a 12s4p, two focboxes and a BMS, or a unity, o didn't choose to make an SS enclosure as it would only hold a 12s2p which might not cut it for the mayority of people.

Hope you guys like it.
```

## \#1232 Posted by: Eboosted Posted at: 2019-02-25T22:27:55.978Z Reads: 303

```
So I‚Äôve been working with @Subsonic_Paul a custom enclosure for their beautiful Century 40 for a couple of months and this is the final outcome.

https://www.eboardsperu.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/02/20190225_154313.jpg
https://www.eboardsperu.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/02/20190225_154306.jpg
https://www.eboardsperu.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/02/20190225_154443.jpg
https://www.eboardsperu.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/02/20190225_154356.jpg

I‚Äôm really proud of the final product as makes this beautiful deck even nicer. The design process was long but worth it, it went back to the drawing board several after several unsuccessful/average attempts.

The Century is a pretty long and wide deck, however it doesn‚Äôt feel too long or wide under your feet. This specific design allowed us to create an enclosure big enough to fit a 13S5P made of 18650 for a maximum discharge of 100A:

![](https://i.imgur.com/k5WdCJq.jpg)

if you use the Samsung 30Qs and, if you are are insane and need a crazy discharge you could fit a 12s4p battery pack made of the newest Samsung 21700 30T cells, that crazy setup will give you 140A of maximum discharge.

https://i.imgur.com/ykqFI0l.jpg
```

```
after a long time looking at the cost and performance of 18650 and 21700 cells i ended up coming to the conclusion that a 12s4p 18650 was the best "bang for buck". 21700 would give more Wh but at an increased cost per Wh and increased weight.
Then at about the same time i as looking kaly made his enclosures available through his website so i ended up ordering 2 of his 18650 enclosures for the carver. he also has a 21700 version but it only fits the hs11/holypro. the kaly enclosure is cheaper but shipping costs more, as i was buying 2 i only pay shipping once.
```

## \#1263 Posted by: b264 Posted at: 2019-04-06T00:35:32.956Z Reads: 264

```
If you go that route, know that arranging a P group down the side like that will require copious amounts of fishpaper between the cells to keep it from vibrating a short into the system.
```

---
## \#1264 Posted by: yelnats8j Posted at: 2019-04-06T00:37:55.551Z Reads: 268

```
It seems like the only way to fit a 10s4p in it.

Is there such thing as too much fish paper?

If not Ill just cover it 2 or 3 times?
```

---
## \#1265 Posted by: b264 Posted at: 2019-04-06T00:40:21.567Z Reads: 269

```
The wires you'll need to run down the sides of the P-group have to be insulated too.  So much insulation.  There isn't really a such thing as too much fishpaper, but beyond 3 layers I'm not sure how much you're gaining.  It's mostly that there will be a bunch of little things that can't touch a bunch of other little things
```

## \#1272 Posted by: Eboosted Posted at: 2019-04-09T06:12:23.777Z Reads: 260

```
A 12s4p is the perfect battery, it will also give you more range than a 10s4p and will accelerate way faster, people always think than going 12s vs 10s will make your board to ride at extreme speeds that's not correct at all, I regularly read people comments saying "I'm not going 12s because I don't plan to run insane speeds", as if the only variable to run fast is the battery and nothing more. 

You could run a really fun board by going 12s and using a really high gear reduction. For instance, on my Sidekick I run 12s5p on 2:1 gear ratio, 190kv motors and 85mm Caguamas, max speed is 51km/hr and the full throttle acceleration puts a smile on my face everyday.
```

---
## \#1273 Posted by: grrsona Posted at: 2019-04-09T06:13:50.626Z Reads: 272

```
What about the strain of 12s on the VESC? 

[quote="b264, post:8, topic:44459, full:true"]
Because the parts used in the vesc circuit shouldn‚Äôt be run that high, especially with a reactive load like motor windings. I‚Äôm not trying to run my controller on the razor edge of what‚Äôs possible because it increases failure rate. I‚Äôd prefer if the board failing on me was kept to an extreme minimum, especially if it means I lose brakes and definitely if it means a $150+ part is the thing failing

Lots of people run at 12S but I also hear of lots of failures. To me, not failing is a very important metric and thus I can‚Äôt consider it. Most consumer electronics are designed with a 40% margin at least, the components in the VESC being rated at 60V and 63V means 8S would meet that criteria, so 10S is already over the normal. 12S is too close
[/quote]
```

---

## \#1280 Posted by: b264 Posted at: 2019-04-09T11:09:36.048Z Reads: 257

```
It's not a myth; the DRV8302 is only rated at 60V.  On applications like this, real engineers never push the parts past 60% to 75% which means 42V, especially driving highly inductive loads (like BLDC motor windings) using square waves (like VESC)

Of course, if it's your face that might hit the street on any malfunctions, you are free to design yours however you'd like to.
```

---
## \#1281 Posted by: City-Blade-101 Posted at: 2019-04-09T13:27:28.159Z Reads: 250

```
@b264 So the new focbox isn't reliable at 12s ?
```

---
## \#1282 Posted by: Eboosted Posted at: 2019-04-09T18:02:23.047Z Reads: 276

```
[quote="b264, post:1280, topic:38073"]
It‚Äôs not a myth; the DRV8302 is only rated at 60V.
[/quote]

You are right, it's not a myth is very frecuent problem found on some 4.12 VESCs when used at 12S and FOC, so my mistake. Nevertheless, from my own experience and several others, I've been pushing FocBoxes for years at 12S and never had any single DRV8302 error to the point I feel pretty confident and happy to suggest people with doubts about going between 10S in BLDC to 12S in FOC, to choose the latest.

[quote="b264, post:1280, topic:38073"]
Of course, if it‚Äôs your face that might hit the street on any malfunctions
[/quote]

My face already hit the streets but it was not because a malfunction caused by designing 12S and FOC on a FocBox, in fact it was a malfunction in BLDC and 10S on my old vanguard.
```

## \#1285 Posted by: finges Posted at: 2019-04-09T22:26:12.623Z Reads: 266

```
Just devils advocating here.. but... 

DRV8302 Spec maxes at 60V
Assuming TI's Electrical Engineers are 'Real Engineers' which means that they would also apply the 60-75% max rule to their component when specc'ing. 

Wouldn't that mean that the DRV8302's real max is 80-100v? Which would also mean that if you took 60-75% off the 60v... you'd really be at like 30-40 percent of the 'real max' rating?
```

## \#1312 Posted by: mikaluch Posted at: 2019-05-14T13:58:10.514Z Reads: 250

```
Those are TKPs.  Engraved with "Blue Shark".  The bushings they came with are too soft for a skating world tank like me.  I'm pushing 90 kilos, not the 70 kilos these things are meant for.  I will put in stiffer bushings (I like the hard insert Bones) but I still think I might need to add risers to keep the widest corners of the enclosure from hitting the ground.

Speaking of sharks, these are the motor mounts @akhlut designed for me.  I love this community.  It is so smoove to tell engineering friends I have parts coming in from around the world for my skateboard.  I'm always quick to mention Peru.

![15577482127641974434421526584975|500x500](upload://894atCHuYA3YRzJQmfFAjxcLMb7.jpeg)
```

## \#1313 Posted by: taz Posted at: 2019-05-14T14:02:28.282Z Reads: 239

```
Aren't the stickers supposed to go to the sides of the enclosure?
```

---
## \#1314 Posted by: mikaluch Posted at: 2019-05-14T14:06:53.134Z Reads: 245

```
They were intended for that.  It is the "Flying Tigers" logo.  The Flying Tigers were three squadrons of fighter pilots and aircraft that volunteered to fight for China against Japan under US command before the US joined WWII.  The logo is cut to go on either side of an aircraft nose.

The height to width ratio only works on the front of the enclosure because of the longer sloped flat there.  I will push the two stickers together.
```

## \#1326 Posted by: rusins Posted at: 2019-05-19T18:11:58.315Z Reads: 234

```
https://securityaffairs.co/wordpress/85683/hacking/wp-live-chat-plugin-bug.html

I think it might be this. Says you need to update the plugin for your Wordpress site to fix the issue.

Why do I think so? Because in the HTML page under the comment "WPLC custom JS" there's a script that gets included. In your browser's dev tools under sources if you open yourservice.live/javascript-mini.js there's a line
`var _td = String.fromCharCode(a bunch of numbers)`
and then the next line evaluates that. Those numbers are just there to obfuscate the malicious script that runs.

I've heard from others in the web dev industry that wordpress sites and their plugins get security flaws like this constantly. If you can, move over to something else in the future :wink:
```

---

```
This is exactly what has happened, I updated the plug in now but the malicious code still remains on the website and I have no idea how to clean it
```

## \#1332 Posted by: rusins Posted at: 2019-05-19T21:05:23.040Z Reads: 238

```
To quote from the article I sent:

> Since ‚Äúadmin_init‚Äù hooks can be called visiting either /wp-admin/admin-post.php or /wp-admin/admin-ajax.php, an unauthenticated attacker could use these endpoints to arbitrarily update the option  ‚Äúwplc_custom_js‚Äù. ‚Äú

So you should go into your site's admin panel or what have you, and find that option (wplc_custom_js) and reset it / remove the attacker's malicious script include / maybe clear it?

Edit: Brent's suggestion is probably the best, you can never be too sure that's the only thing the attackers had access to.

Edit no. 2: Realized there's a [dedicated thread about this.](https://www.electric-skateboard.builders/t/looking-for-help-from-web-experts/94344/6) Whoops. Mods can move these messages over to there if they care.
```

## \#1364 Posted by: Eboosted Posted at: 2019-06-17T21:50:50.518Z Reads: 221

```
Hello guys, I'm pretty excited to release the new HS11/HolyPro SS enclosure for 20700/21700 cells.

This enclosure request has been made so many times I lost count, this was a challenge to create because the Trampa HS11/HolyPro deck is very narrow and the length was not ideal to fit 21700 cells. However, I was able to completely redesign this enclosure from scratch and made it long enough to hold a 12S4P made of 21700 cells.

The design has an extended flare on the nose and tail, which not only allows to increase the pockets length but to help a perfect seal for waterproofing making it ideal for rainy days.

Now you can fit Samsung 30Ts for an insane 140A of discharge on a just a single stack slim enclosure, Sanyo 20700s can also be used and they fit like a glove.

[img]https://i.imgur.com/wZLTJ81.jpg[/img]
[img]https://i.imgur.com/2p7Q2G0.jpg[/img]
[img]https://i.imgur.com/ZrpPSFd.jpg[/img]
[img]https://i.imgur.com/U7gdUaq.jpg[/img]
[img]https://i.imgur.com/H0ysPAe.jpg[/img]
[img]https://i.imgur.com/VqxLWgW.jpg[/img]
[img]https://i.imgur.com/XlhXLkB.jpg[/img]
[img]https://i.imgur.com/04rRVcf.jpg[/img]
[img]https://i.imgur.com/dj5irzU.jpg[/img]
```

## \#1415 Posted by: Eboosted Posted at: 2019-08-07T22:48:44.155Z Reads: 166

```
I'm sorry about this but your project needs a really thick enclosure, not all enclosures look good on double stack, the deck needs to have curves and subtle shapes in order for the enclosure to to make it flow and look good such as the Evo DS or Trampa HS11 DS.

That's why I decided to make a 12S4P 21700 on the switchblade single stack
```
